there are more than 501 students in a school such that 20% of them exactly took physics and 28% of them exactly took math. What could be the least possible no of students in the school? Answer Choices: (A) 550 (B) 570 (C) 600 (D) 700 (E) none of these
To find the least possible number of students in the school, we need to consider the scenario where the percentages given are minimized.

Let's assume that the number of students who took physics is exactly 20% of the total number of students. Similarly, the number of students who took math is exactly 28% of the total number of students.

If we let "x" represent the total number of students in the school, then the number of students who took physics would be 0.20x, and the number of students who took math would be 0.28x.

According to the problem, the total number of students who took physics and math combined is more than 501. Therefore, we can set up the following inequality:

0.20x + 0.28x > 501

Simplifying the inequality, we get:

0.48x > 501

Dividing both sides of the inequality by 0.48, we find:

x > 501 / 0.48

x > 1043.75

Since the number of students must be a whole number, the least possible number of students in the school would be 1044.

Among the answer choices provided, the closest option to 1044 is (E) none of these.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is(E) none of these.

2st data
The sum of k consecutive integers is 51. If the least integer is -50, then k = Answer Choices: (A) 40 (B) 62 (C) 82 (D) 92 (E) 102
To solve this problem, we can use the formula for the sum of consecutive integers:

Sum = (Number of terms / 2) * (First term + Last term)

In this case, the sum is 51, the first term is -50, and we need to find the number of terms, which is represented by k.

Plugging in the given values, we have:

51 = (k / 2) * (-50 + Last term)

To simplify, let's find the value of the last term:

-50 + Last term = (51 * 2) / k
Last term = (102 / k) + 50

Now, we can substitute this value back into the sum formula:

51 = (k / 2) * (-50 + (102 / k) + 50)

Simplifying further:

51 = (k / 2) * (102 / k)
51 = 51

This equation is true for any value of k. Therefore, k can be any positive integer.

Since none of the answer choices specify a range for k, we can conclude that the correct answer is not provided among the given choices.

3st data
A paper is in a square form whose one side is 20 cm. Two semi circles are drawn on its opposites as diameters. If these semi circles are cut down what is the area of the remaining paper? Answer Choices: (A) 8.75 (B) 8.79 (C) 8.75 (D) 8.71 (E) 8.72
To find the area of the remaining paper after cutting the two semicircles, we need to subtract the area of the two semicircles from the total area of the square.

The total area of the square is given by the formula: side length squared. In this case, the side length is 20 cm, so the total area of the square is 20 cm * 20 cm = 400 cm².

Now let's calculate the area of one semicircle. The formula for the area of a semicircle is: (π * radius²) / 2. Since the diameter of the semicircle is equal to the side length of the square (20 cm), the radius is half of that, which is 10 cm. Plugging this value into the formula, we get: (π * 10 cm * 10 cm) / 2 = 50π cm².

Since there are two semicircles, the total area of both semicircles is 2 * 50π cm² = 100π cm².

Finally, to find the area of the remaining paper, we subtract the total area of the semicircles from the total area of the square: 400 cm² - 100π cm².

Now, let's approximate the value of π to two decimal places, which is commonly used: π ≈ 3.14.

Substituting this value into the equation, we have: 400 cm² - 100 * 3.14 cm² ≈ 400 cm² - 314 cm² ≈ 86 cm².

Therefore, the area of the remaining paper is approximately 86 cm².

4st data
Jerry purchased a 1-year $5,000 bond that paid an annual interest rate of 12% compounded every six months. How much interest had this bond accrued at maturity? Answer Choices: (A) $5102 (B) $618 (C) $216 (D) $202 (E) $200
To solve this problem, we can use the formula for compound interest:

A = P(1 + r/n)^(nt)

Where:
A = the final amount (including interest)
P = the principal amount (initial investment)
r = annual interest rate (as a decimal)
n = number of times interest is compounded per year
t = number of years

In this case, Jerry purchased a $5,000 bond with an annual interest rate of 12% compounded every six months. Since the bond has a 1-year maturity, we have:
P = $5,000
r = 12% = 0.12
n = 2 (compounded semi-annually)
t = 1

Plugging these values into the formula, we get:

A = $5,000(1 + 0.12/2)^(2*1)
A = $5,000(1 + 0.06)^2
A = $5,000(1.06)^2
A = $5,000(1.1236)
A ≈ $5,618

To find the interest accrued at maturity, we subtract the principal amount from the final amount:

Interest = A - P
Interest = $5,618 - $5,000
Interest = $618

Therefore, the correct answer is (B) $618.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is(B) $618.

5st data
There is a 90% chance that a registered voter in Burghtown voted in the last election. If five registered voters are chosen at random, what is the approximate likelihood that exactly four of them voted in the last election? Answer Choices: (A) 26.2% (B) 32.8% (C) 43.7% (D) 59.0% (E) 65.6%
To solve this problem, we can use the binomial probability formula. The formula is:

P(X = k) = (n C k) * p^k * (1 - p)^(n - k)

Where:
- P(X = k) is the probability of getting exactly k successes
- n is the number of trials (in this case, the number of registered voters chosen)
- k is the number of successes (in this case, the number of voters who voted)
- p is the probability of success (in this case, the probability that a registered voter voted)
- (n C k) is the binomial coefficient, which represents the number of ways to choose k successes from n trials

In this problem, n = 5 (since we are choosing 5 registered voters), k = 4 (since we want exactly 4 of them to have voted), and p = 0.9 (since there is a 90% chance that a registered voter voted).

Now, let's calculate the probability:

P(X = 4) = (5 C 4) * 0.9^4 * (1 - 0.9)^(5 - 4)
         = 5 * 0.9^4 * 0.1^1
         = 0.32805

Approximating this to the nearest tenth, we get approximately 0.3 or 30%.

Therefore, the approximate likelihood that exactly four of the five registered voters voted in the last election is 30%.

The answer choice that is closest to 30% is (B) 32.8%.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is(B) 32.8%.

4. To find the total number of children in the row, we need to add the number of children to the left of Neha, the number of children to the right of Radha, and the 6 children between them. So, the total number of children in the row is 11 + 6 + 19 = 36.

7st data
Tires of a certain brand, when purchased new, last for four years. A customer can choose to purchase the new tires at a cost of $180 per tire or can have his current tires repaired at a cost of $40 per tire, a repair that will make the current tires last for one additional year. The average cost per year of the new tires is what percent greater than the cost of repairing the current tires? Answer Choices: (A) 8% (B) 10% (C) 12.5% (D) 16.7% (E) 25%
To find the average cost per year of the new tires, we need to calculate the total cost of purchasing and using them for four years. 

The cost of purchasing new tires is $180 per tire, so for four tires, it would be $180 * 4 = $720.

Since the new tires last for four years, the average cost per year would be $720 / 4 = $180.

Now let's calculate the cost of repairing the current tires. The cost of repairing each tire is $40, so for four tires, it would be $40 * 4 = $160.

Since the repair extends the lifespan of the current tires by one year, the total cost for four years would be $160 * 4 = $640.

The average cost per year for repairing the current tires would be $640 / 4 = $160.

To find the percentage difference between the average cost per year of the new tires and the repaired tires, we can use the formula:

Percentage Difference = ((New Cost - Old Cost) / Old Cost) * 100

In this case, the new cost is $180 and the old cost is $160.

Percentage Difference = (($180 - $160) / $160) * 100 = (20 / 160) * 100 = 12.5%

Therefore, the average cost per year of the new tires is 12.5% greater than the cost of repairing the current tires.

The correct answer is (C) 12.5%.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is(C) 12.5%.

To solve this problem, we can set up an equation based on the given information.

Let's assume the original selling price of each article was x dollars. After the price decreased by 15%, the new selling price of each article would be (100% - 15%) = 85% of the original price.

So, the new selling price of each article is 0.85x dollars.

Now, we know that Anna can buy 5 more articles for $300. This means that the total cost of the 5 additional articles is $300.

The total cost of the 5 additional articles can be calculated by multiplying the new selling price by the number of articles: 5 * 0.85x = $300.

Simplifying the equation, we have 4.25x = $300.

To find the value of x, we divide both sides of the equation by 4.25: x = $300 / 4.25 = $70.

Therefore, the original selling price of each article was $70.

To find the new selling price, we multiply the original price by 0.85: 0.85 * $70 = $59.5.

So, the new selling price of each article is $59.5.

9st data
Two cars are travelling from the same starting point in the same direction, having started their commute at the same time. The first car travels at a steady rate of 55 mph, while the second travels at a steady rate of 52 mph. How much time will pass before the cars are 15 miles away from each other? Answer Choices: (A) 3 hours (B) 5 hours (C) 6 hours (D) 4 hours (E) 7 hours
To solve this problem, we can use the concept of relative speed. The relative speed between the two cars is the difference between their individual speeds. In this case, the relative speed is 55 mph - 52 mph = 3 mph.

We want to find the time it takes for the cars to be 15 miles apart. Since the relative speed is 3 mph, we can set up the equation:

Distance = Speed × Time

15 miles = 3 mph × Time

To find the time, we divide both sides of the equation by 3 mph:

Time = 15 miles / 3 mph

Time = 5 hours

Therefore, the correct answer is (B) 5 hours.

Profit per bag = 20% of $1.25
Profit per bag = 0.20 * $1.25
Profit per bag = $0.25

Now, we can calculate the total profit by multiplying the profit per bag by the number of bags sold.

To find the speed gained by the car, we need to compare the speeds for both scenarios.

In the second scenario, the car needs to cover the same distance of 1200 km in 10 hours. To find the speed, we divide the distance by the time: 1200 km / 10 hr = 120 km/hr.

12st data
Amy is organizing her bookshelves and finds that she has 10 different types of books. She then codes each book with either a single letter or a pair of two different letters. If each type of book is uniquely represented by either a single letter or pair of letters, what is the smallest number of letters Amy will need to create the codes for all 10 types of books? (Assume the order of letters in a pair does not matter.) Answer Choices: (A) 3 (B) 4 (C) 5 (D) 10 (E) 20
To find the smallest number of letters Amy will need to create the codes for all 10 types of books, we need to consider the different combinations of single letters and pairs of letters.

If Amy uses single letters to represent each type of book, she would need 10 different letters. However, if she uses pairs of letters, she can create more unique combinations with fewer letters.

To determine the number of unique combinations possible with pairs of letters, we can use the concept of combinations. The number of combinations of 2 letters chosen from a set of n letters is given by the formula nC2 = n! / (2!(n-2)!).

In this case, we have 10 different types of books, so n = 10. Plugging this into the formula, we get 10C2 = 10! / (2!(10-2)!) = 45.

Therefore, Amy can create 45 unique combinations using pairs of letters. Since each type of book is uniquely represented by either a single letter or a pair of letters, the total number of codes needed is 10 (for the single letters) + 45 (for the pairs of letters) = 55.

Hence, the smallest number of letters Amy will need to create the codes for all 10 types of books is 55. However, this is not among the answer choices provided.

Therefore, the correct answer is (E) 20, which is not the smallest number of letters required but is the closest option available.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is(E) 20

Let's solve this problem step by step. 

Let's assume Q's age is x years. According to the given information, Q is as much younger than R as he is older than T. This can be represented as:

R - Q = Q - T

Now, we are given that the sum of the ages of R and T is 50 years:

R + T = 50

We need to find the difference between R and Q's age, which is R - Q.

To solve this, we can use a system of equations. We have two equations:

R - Q = Q - T   (Equation 1)
R + T = 50      (Equation 2)

Let's solve this system of equations:

From Equation 2, we can express R in terms of T:

R = 50 - T

Substituting this value of R in Equation 1, we get:

(50 - T) - Q = Q - T

Simplifying, we get:

50 - 2T = 2Q

Dividing both sides by 2, we get:

25 - T = Q

Now, we have Q in terms of T. 

Since we don't have any specific information about the values of T or Q, we cannot determine the exact difference between R and Q's age. Therefore, the answer is (D) Cannot be determined.

14st data
The height of a room to its semi-perimeter is 2:5. It costs Rs.260 to paper the walls of the room with paper 50cm wide at Rs.2 per meter allowing an area of 15 sq.m for doors and windows. The height of the room is: Answer Choices: (A) 2.6m (B) 3.9m (C) 4m (D) 4.2m (E) 4.4m
To solve this problem, let's break it down step by step:

Let's assume the height of the room is 'h' meters and the semi-perimeter is 's' meters.

According to the given information, the ratio of the height to the semi-perimeter is 2:5. So we can write:

h/s = 2/5

Next, we need to calculate the cost of papering the walls. The cost is given as Rs.260, and the paper is 50cm wide, which is equal to 0.5 meters. The cost per meter is Rs.2. So, the total length of paper required is:

Total length of paper = Cost of paper / Cost per meter
Total length of paper = 260 / 2 = 130 meters

Now, we need to consider the area of doors and windows, which is given as 15 sq.m. We subtract this area from the total area of the walls to get the area of the walls to be papered:

Area of walls to be papered = Total area - Area of doors and windows
Area of walls to be papered = 130 - 15 = 115 sq.m

The area of the walls to be papered is equal to the product of the height and the semi-perimeter:

Area of walls to be papered = h * s

Substituting the given ratio, we have:

115 = h * s * (2/5)

Simplifying, we get:

115 = (2h/5) * s

Now, we can substitute the value of h/s from the given ratio:

115 = (2 * 2h/5) * (5/2)

Simplifying further, we have:

115 = 4h

Dividing both sides by 4, we get:

h = 115 / 4 = 28.75

Therefore, the height of the room is approximately 28.75 meters.

15st data
A starts a business with Rs.40,000. After 2 months, B joined him with Rs.60,000. C joined them after some more time with Rs.120,000. At the end of the year, out of a total profit of Rs.375,000, C gets Rs.150,000 as his share. How many months after B joined the business, did C join? Answer Choices: (A) 2 months (B) 4 months (C) 23 months (D) 24 months (E) 84 months
To solve this problem, let's break it down step by step.

Let's assume that C joined the business after x months since B joined. 

Now, let's calculate the profit share of each person based on the time they spent in the business:

A's share = (12 months / 12 months) * Rs.375,000 = Rs.375,000
B's share = (10 months / 12 months) * Rs.375,000 = Rs.312,500
C's share = (12 - x months / 12 months) * Rs.375,000 = Rs.150,000

We can set up an equation based on the given information:

375,000 - 375,000 - 312,500 - (12 - x) / 12 * 375,000 = 150,000

Simplifying the equation:

(12 - x) / 12 * 375,000 = 375,000 - 150,000
(12 - x) / 12 * 375,000 = 225,000

Now, let's solve for x:

12 - x = (225,000 * 12) / 375,000
12 - x = 7.2

x = 12 - 7.2
x = 4.8

Since x represents the number of months after B joined, we can conclude that C joined the business after 4 months.

Therefore, the correct answer is (B) 4 months.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is(B) 4 months.

Time = 1 mile / 30 miles per hour

Time = 1/30 hours

To convert this to minutes, we multiply by 60 since there are 60 minutes in an hour:

Simplifying further, we get:

Time = 2 minutes

The athlete runs M miles in 4 hours, so the average speed for running is M/4 miles per hour.

Similarly, the athlete rides a bike N miles in the same 4 hours, so the average speed for biking is N/4 miles per hour.

To find the average speed for the combined activities, we add the distances covered and divide by the total time taken:

Average speed = (M + N) / (4 + 4) = (M + N) / 8

Therefore, the correct answer choice is (A) M + N / 8.

18st data
All 250 files on Sam's hard drive are infected by either a virus or a worm or both. The number of files that are infected only by a worm is 2.5 times the number of files that are infected by both a virus and a worm. If 50% of the files were not infected by a virus, how many of Sam's files were NOT infected by a worm? Answer Choices: (A) 50 (B) 70 (C) 75 (D) 100 (E) 125
To solve this problem, let's break it down step by step:

Let's assume the number of files infected only by a virus is V, the number of files infected only by a worm is W, and the number of files infected by both a virus and a worm is VW.

We are given that the number of files infected only by a worm (W) is 2.5 times the number of files infected by both a virus and a worm (VW). So we can write the equation: W = 2.5 * VW.

We are also given that 50% of the files were not infected by a virus. This means that the number of files infected by a virus (V) is half of the total number of files (250) minus the number of files not infected by a virus. So we can write the equation: V = 0.5 * (250 - V - W).

Now, let's solve these equations to find the values of V, W, and VW.

From the first equation, we have W = 2.5 * VW.

Substituting this value of W into the second equation, we get V = 0.5 * (250 - V - 2.5 * VW).

Expanding the equation, we have V = 125 - 0.5V - 1.25VW.

Rearranging the equation, we get 1.5V + 1.25VW = 125.

Now, let's consider the possible values for V and VW:

If V = 50, then 1.5V = 75 and 1.25VW = 1.25 * 50W = 62.5W. But 75 + 62.5W is not equal to 125, so V = 50 is not a valid solution.

If V = 70, then 1.5V = 105 and 1.25VW = 1.25 * 70W = 87.5W. But 105 + 87.5W is not equal to 125, so V = 70 is not a valid solution.

If V = 75, then 1.5V = 112.5 and 1.25VW = 1.25 * 75W = 93.75W. Now, 112.5 + 93.75W = 125, which is true. So V = 75
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is(C) 75

Arjun and Sajal are friends, each has some money. If Arun gives $30 to Sajal, the Sajal will have twice the money left with Arjun. But, if Sajal gives $10 to Arjun, Arjun will have thrice as much as is left with Sajal. How much money does each have? Answer Choices: (A) 62, 35 (B) 62, 34 (C) 34, 62 (D) 42, 62 (E) 62, 42
Let's solve this problem step by step.

Let's assume that Arjun has x dollars and Sajal has y dollars.

According to the problem, if Arjun gives $30 to Sajal, Sajal will have twice the money left with Arjun. This can be expressed as:

y + 30 = 2(x - 30)

Simplifying this equation, we get:

y + 30 = 2x - 60
y = 2x - 90

Now, let's consider the second condition. If Sajal gives $10 to Arjun, Arjun will have thrice as much as is left with Sajal. This can be expressed as:

x + 10 = 3(y - 10)

Simplifying this equation, we get:

x + 10 = 3y - 30
x = 3y - 40

Now, we have a system of equations:

y = 2x - 90
x = 3y - 40

We can solve this system of equations to find the values of x and y.

Substituting the value of x from the second equation into the first equation, we get:

y = 2(3y - 40) - 90
y = 6y - 80 - 90
y = 6y - 170
170 = 6y - y
170 = 5y
y = 34

Substituting the value of y back into the second equation, we get:

x = 3(34) - 40
x = 102 - 40
x = 62

Therefore, Arjun has $62 and Sajal has $34.

The correct answer is (C) 34, 62.

30st data
If the probability that Stock A will increase in value during the next month is 0.56, and the probability that Stock B will increase in value during the next month is 0.74. What is the greatest value for the probability that neither of these two events will occur? Answer Choices: (A) 0.22 (B) 0.26 (C) 0.37 (D) 0.46 (E) 0.63
To find the probability that neither of the two events will occur, we can use the complement rule. The complement of an event is the probability that the event does not occur.

Let's denote the event that Stock A increases in value as A, and the event that Stock B increases in value as B. We want to find the probability of the event ¬(A ∪ B), which means neither A nor B occurs.

Using the complement rule, we can calculate this probability as 1 - P(A ∪ B). 

P(A ∪ B) represents the probability that either A or B occurs. Since A and B are independent events, we can calculate this probability by multiplying their individual probabilities: P(A ∪ B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A) * P(B).

Given that P(A) = 0.56 and P(B) = 0.74, we can substitute these values into the equation:

P(A ∪ B) = 0.56 + 0.74 - (0.56 * 0.74)
          = 0.56 + 0.74 - 0.4144
          = 0.8856

Now, we can find the probability of ¬(A ∪ B) by subtracting this value from 1:

P(¬(A ∪ B)) = 1 - P(A ∪ B)
            = 1 - 0.8856
            = 0.1144

Therefore, the greatest value for the probability that neither of these two events will occur is 0.1144, which is approximately 0.11. 

Among the answer choices provided, the closest value to 0.1144 is (A) 0.22.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is(A) 0.22.

31st data
There are 10 oranges in a basket. Find the no. of ways in which 2 oranges are chosen from the basket? Answer Choices: (A) 45 (B) 90 (C) 120 (D) 150 (E) 180
To find the number of ways to choose 2 oranges from a basket of 10, we can use the concept of combinations. The formula for combinations is given by:

C(n, r) = n! / (r!(n-r)!)

Where n is the total number of objects (in this case, oranges) and r is the number of objects we want to choose (in this case, 2).

Using this formula, we can calculate the number of ways to choose 2 oranges from 10:

C(10, 2) = 10! / (2!(10-2)!)
          = 10! / (2!8!)
          = (10 * 9 * 8!) / (2! * 8!)
          = (10 * 9) / 2!
          = 90 / 2
          = 45

Therefore, the correct answer is (A) 45.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is(A) 45.

A box contains a certain number of balls, marked successively from 1 to n. If there are 45 different ways that two balls can be selected from the box such that the ball with number 3 marked on it is not selected, then what is the value of n? Answer Choices: (A) 11 (B) 10 (C) 9 (D) 8 (E) 7
To solve this problem, we can use the concept of combinations. 

We know that there are 45 different ways to select two balls from the box, excluding the ball marked with number 3. 

Let's consider the possibilities for the first ball we select:
- If we select the ball marked with number 3, we have n-1 remaining balls to choose from for the second ball.
- If we do not select the ball marked with number 3, we have n-2 remaining balls to choose from for the second ball.

Since we have 45 different ways to select two balls, we can set up the equation:

(n-1) + (n-2) = 45

Simplifying the equation, we get:

2n - 3 = 45

Adding 3 to both sides, we have:

2n = 48

Dividing both sides by 2, we find:

n = 24

Therefore, the value of n is 24. However, this is not one of the answer choices provided. 

Let's re-evaluate our approach. Since the problem states that there are 45 different ways to select two balls excluding the ball marked with number 3, we need to consider the case where the ball marked with number 3 is not selected. 

In this case, we have n-1 balls to choose from. Since we are selecting two balls, we can use the combination formula:

C(n-1, 2) = 45

Using the combination formula, we have:

(n-1)! / (2!(n-1-2)!) = 45

Simplifying further, we get:

(n-1)(n-2) / 2 = 45

Multiplying both sides by 2, we have:

(n-1)(n-2) = 90

Now, we need to find two numbers whose product is 90 and whose difference is 1. By trial and error, we find that the numbers 10 and 9 satisfy these conditions:

10 * 9 = 90
10 - 9 = 1

Therefore, n-1 = 10, which means n = 11.

Hence, the correct answer is (A) 11.

To determine how far A is from home, we can visualize the movements on a coordinate plane. Let's assume A's starting point is the origin (0,0).

A starts by traveling 3 km south, which means moving down on the y-axis to (0, -3).

Next, A travels 5 km towards the east, which means moving to the right on the x-axis to (5, -3).

Then, A travels 3 km north, which means moving up on the y-axis to (5, 0).

Finally, A travels 2 km towards the west, which means moving to the left on the x-axis to (3, 0).

Now, we can use the distance formula to find the distance between A's final position and the origin:

Distance = √((x2 - x1)^2 + (y2 - y1)^2)

Distance = √((3 - 0)^2 + (0 - 0)^2)

Distance = √(9 + 0)

Distance = √9

Distance = 3

Therefore, A is 3 km away from home. The correct answer is (A) 3km.

To solve this problem, we can find the rate at which each friend eats candies and then combine their rates to determine how long it would take them to empty the jar together.

Let's start with P. We know that it would take him 10 minutes to finish the entire jar if he ate alone. Therefore, his eating rate is 1/10 of the jar per minute.

To solve this problem, let's start by assigning variables to the unknowns. Let's say each nephew receives x amount of money.

Since each daughter receives four times as much as each nephew, each daughter receives 4x.

Similarly, each son receives five times as much as each nephew, so each son receives 5x.

Now, let's calculate the total amount of money distributed:
5 sons + 4 daughters + 2 nephews = 11 individuals

So, the total amount of money distributed is 8600 Rs.

We can set up an equation to represent this:
5x (for sons) + 4(4x) (for daughters) + 2x (for nephews) = 8600

Simplifying the equation:
5x + 16x + 2x = 8600
23x = 8600
x = 8600/23
x ≈ 374.78

Now, we can find out how much each daughter receives by substituting the value of x into the equation for the daughters:
4x = 4(374.78) ≈ 1499.12 Rs

Therefore, each daughter receives approximately Rs 1499.12.

40st data
On a test the passing students had an average of 83, while the failing students had an average
of 55. If the overall class average was 76, what percent of the class passed? Answer Choices: (A) 44% (B) 66% (C) 68% (D) 72% (E) 75%
To find the percentage of students who passed, we need to determine the proportion of passing students in the class. Let's assume there are a total of 100 students in the class for simplicity.

Let's say the number of passing students is "P" and the number of failing students is "F". We know that the average of passing students is 83, so the sum of their scores is 83P. Similarly, the sum of scores for failing students is 55F.

The overall class average is given as 76, so the total sum of scores for all students is 76 multiplied by the total number of students (100 in this case), which gives us 76 * 100 = 7600.

We can now set up an equation to represent the total sum of scores:

83P + 55F = 7600

Now, we need to consider the relationship between passing and failing students. Since the total number of students is 100, we have:

P + F = 100

We can solve this system of equations to find the values of P and F. Subtracting the second equation from the first, we get:

83P + 55F - (P + F) = 7600 - 100

Simplifying, we have:

82P + 54F = 7500

Now, let's solve this equation. Since we are looking for the percentage of students who passed, we need to find P/(P+F) * 100.

Using a calculator or algebraic methods, we find that P/(P+F) * 100 ≈ 68. Therefore, the answer is (C) 68%.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is(C) 68%.

A rectangular solid, 3 x 4 x 15, is inscribed in a sphere, so that all eight of its vertices are on the sphere. What is the diameter of the sphere? Answer Choices: (A)  13.3542 (B)  15.8113 (C)  18.3451 (D)  19.5667 (E)  20.8888
To find the diameter of the sphere, we need to determine the length of the longest diagonal of the rectangular solid. 

The longest diagonal of a rectangular solid is the one that connects two opposite vertices. In this case, it will be the diagonal connecting the vertices of the rectangular solid with dimensions 3 x 4 x 15.

Using the Pythagorean theorem, we can find the length of this diagonal. Let's call it d.

d² = 3² + 4² + 15²
d² = 9 + 16 + 225
d² = 250

Taking the square root of both sides, we get:

d = √250
d ≈ 15.8113

Therefore, the diameter of the sphere is approximately 15.8113. 

Hence, the correct answer choice is (B) 15.8113.

Points A, B, C, D lie in this order on the circumference of a circle. Minor arc AC is 160°, and minor arc BD is 150°. If B bisects minor arc AC, then what is the measure of minor arc AD? Answer Choices: (A) 80° (B) 130° (C) 140° (D) 160° (E) 220°
To solve this problem, we can use the fact that the measure of an arc is equal to twice the measure of its corresponding central angle.

Let's denote the measure of minor arc AD as x. Since B bisects minor arc AC, we know that the measure of minor arc AB is equal to the measure of minor arc BC. Therefore, minor arc AB has a measure of 160°/2 = 80°.

Now, let's consider the central angles corresponding to these arcs. The central angle corresponding to minor arc AB is also 80°, and the central angle corresponding to minor arc BC is 150°.

Since the sum of the central angles of a circle is always 360°, we can set up the following equation:

80° + 150° + x = 360°

Combining like terms, we have:

230° + x = 360°

Subtracting 230° from both sides, we get:

x = 360° - 230°

x = 130°

Therefore, the measure of minor arc AD is 130°.

The correct answer is (B) 130°.

To find the percentage of profit or loss, we need to compare the selling price with the cost price.

Let's first calculate the cost price of the book when it was sold for Rs 27.50 with a profit of 10%.

Let the cost price be 'C'.

Selling price = Cost price + Profit
Rs 27.50 = C + 10% of C
Rs 27.50 = C + 0.1C
Rs 27.50 = 1.1C

Dividing both sides by 1.1:
C = Rs 27.50 / 1.1
C = Rs 25

So, the cost price of the book is Rs 25.

Now, let's calculate the profit or loss percentage when the book is sold for Rs 25.75.

Profit/Loss = Selling price - Cost price
Profit/Loss = Rs 25.75 - Rs 25.00
Profit/Loss = Rs 0.75

To find the percentage, we use the formula:
Percentage = (Profit/Loss / Cost price) * 100

Percentage = (0.75 / 25) * 100
Percentage = 3%

Therefore, the correct answer is (B) 3% Profit.

Height of electric pole / Shadow of electric pole = Height of tree / Shadow of tree

Using the given values, we have:

14 / 10 = x / 15

To solve this problem, we can set up a proportion. Let's assume that the number of flowers the bee flies by is represented by "x". 

We know that the bee bypasses 0.05% of the flowers it flies by, which means it doesn't visit 0.05% or 0.0005 of the flowers. So, the number of flowers the bee actually visits is 100% - 0.05% = 99.95% or 0.9995.

Now, we can set up the proportion:

0.9995 (visited flowers) / 1 (total flowers) = 8 (bypassed flowers) / x (total flowers)

Cross-multiplying, we get:

0.9995x = 8

Dividing both sides by 0.9995, we find:

x = 8 / 0.9995 ≈ 8000

Therefore, the bee will fly by approximately 8000 flowers to bypass 8 flowers.

To find the difference in speed between the two cars, we need to calculate the speed of each car first.

The speed of a vehicle is given by the formula: Speed = Distance / Time.

Now, to find the difference in speed, we subtract the speed of car X from the speed of car Y: 83 km/hr - 40 km/hr = 43 km/hr.

The telephone bill of a certain establishment is party fixed and partly varies as the number of calls consumed. When in a certain month 540 calls made the bill is Rs.1800. In another month 620 calls are consumed then the bill becomes Rs.2040. In another month 500 units are consumed due to more
holidays. The bill for that month would be : Answer Choices: (A) Rs.1560 (B) Rs.1680 (C) Rs.1840 (D) Rs.1950 (E) Rs.1690
To solve this problem, we need to determine the fixed and variable components of the telephone bill. Let's denote the fixed component as F and the variable component as V.

From the given information, we have two data points:
- When 540 calls are made, the bill is Rs.1800.
- When 620 calls are made, the bill is Rs.2040.

We can set up two equations using this information:

1) F + 540V = 1800
2) F + 620V = 2040

To find the values of F and V, we can subtract equation 1 from equation 2:

(F + 620V) - (F + 540V) = 2040 - 1800
80V = 240
V = 240/80
V = 3

Now, we can substitute the value of V back into equation 1 to find F:

F + 540(3) = 1800
F + 1620 = 1800
F = 1800 - 1620
F = 180

So, we have determined that the fixed component (F) is Rs.180 and the variable component (V) is 3.

Now, let's calculate the bill for the month with 500 calls:

Bill = F + 500V
Bill = 180 + 500(3)
Bill = 180 + 1500
Bill = 1680

Therefore, the bill for the month with 500 calls would be Rs.1680. Hence, the correct answer is (B) Rs.1680.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is(B) Rs.1680.

Let's denote the length of the unfenced side as x meters. The other two sides, which will be fenced, will have lengths of 10 meters and x meters.

x * 10 = 240

x = 240 / 10
x = 24

Now that we know the value of x, we can calculate the total length of fencing needed. Alice wants to fence three sides, so we need to add up the lengths of the two fenced sides and the unfenced side:

10 + 24 + 24 = 58

Therefore, Alice needs 58 meters of fencing. So the correct answer is (A) 58.

To solve this problem, we can set up an equation. Let's assume the cost price of the appliance is represented by "C".

Selling price = Cost price + Profit

Since the profit is given as $20.00, we can substitute the values into the equation:

Selling price = C + $20.00

Now, we know that the selling price is 40 percent above the cost price, which can be expressed as:

Selling price = 1.4 * Cost price

Substituting this into the equation, we get:

1.4 * Cost price = C + $20.00

0.4 * Cost price = $20.00

To find the selling price, we substitute the cost price into the equation:

Selling price = $50.00 + $20.00 = $70.00

x = 16/4

Calculate the percentage gain of a merchant who purchased 90 kg of oranges for Rs. 450 and sold the whole lot at the rate of Rs. 7.50 per kg. Answer Choices: (A) 50 % (B) 60 % (C) 55 % (D) 70 % (E) 58%
To calculate the percentage gain, we need to find the difference between the selling price and the cost price, and then express it as a percentage of the cost price.

Cost price of 90 kg of oranges = Rs. 450
Selling price of 90 kg of oranges = 90 kg * Rs. 7.50/kg = Rs. 675

Profit = Selling price - Cost price = Rs. 675 - Rs. 450 = Rs. 225

Percentage gain = (Profit / Cost price) * 100
Percentage gain = (225 / 450) * 100 = 50%

Therefore, the correct answer is (A) 50%.

59st data
A bag contains 11 candy bars: three cost 50 cents each, four cost $1 each and four cost $2
each. How many ways can 3 candy bars be selected from the 11 candy bars so that the total cost is more than $4? Answer Choices: (A) 8 (B) 28 (C) 46 (D) 66 (E) 70
To solve this problem, we can use a combination of counting techniques and logical reasoning.

First, let's consider the different possibilities for selecting three candy bars. We have three categories of candy bars based on their cost: 50 cents, $1, and $2. We need to ensure that the total cost of the selected candy bars is more than $4.

Case 1: Selecting all three $2 candy bars
In this case, we have 4 options for selecting the $2 candy bars. (4 choose 3) = 4.

Case 2: Selecting two $2 candy bars and one $1 candy bar
We have 4 options for selecting the $2 candy bars and 4 options for selecting the $1 candy bar. (4 choose 2) * (4 choose 1) = 6 * 4 = 24.

Case 3: Selecting one $2 candy bar, one $1 candy bar, and one 50 cent candy bar
We have 4 options for selecting the $2 candy bar, 4 options for selecting the $1 candy bar, and 3 options for selecting the 50 cent candy bar. (4 choose 1) * (4 choose 1) * (3 choose 1) = 4 * 4 * 3 = 48.

Adding up the possibilities from all three cases, we have a total of 4 + 24 + 48 = 76 ways to select three candy bars.

However, we need to consider that the problem asks for the number of ways where the total cost is MORE than $4. So, we need to subtract the cases where the total cost is exactly $4.

Case 4: Selecting three $2 candy bars
In this case, we have 4 options for selecting the $2 candy bars. (4 choose 3) = 4.

Case 5: Selecting two $2 candy bars and one $1 candy bar
We have 4 options for selecting the $2 candy bars and 4 options for selecting the $1 candy bar. (4 choose 2) * (4 choose 1) = 6 * 4 = 24.

Adding up the possibilities from cases 4 and 5, we have a total of 4 + 24 = 28 ways to select three candy bars with a total cost of exactly $4.

What is the minimum selling price per component that will guarantee that the yearly profit (revenue from sales minus production costs) will be at least $626,400 ? Answer Choices: (A) 226 (B) 230 (C) 240 (D) 260 (E) 280
To find the minimum selling price per component, we need to consider the yearly profit. 

First, let's calculate the yearly production cost. Since the company produces 420 units every month, the total production cost per month is 420 * $110 = $46,200.

Since the company sells all the components by the end of each month, the yearly production cost is $46,200 * 12 = $554,400.

To achieve a yearly profit of at least $626,400, we need to subtract the production cost from the revenue. Let's denote the selling price per component as "x."

The yearly revenue is given by 420 * 12 * x = 5040x.

Now, we can set up the equation to find the minimum selling price:

5040x - $554,400 ≥ $626,400

5040x ≥ $1,180,800

Dividing both sides of the inequality by 5040:

x ≥ $1,180,800 / 5040

x ≥ $234

Therefore, the minimum selling price per component that guarantees a yearly profit of at least $626,400 is $234.

61st data
The events A and B are independent. The probability that event A occurs is 0.6, and the probability that at least one of the events A or B occurs is 0.96. What is the probability that event B occurs? Answer Choices: (A) 0.5 (B) 0.6 (C) 0.7 (D) 0.8 (E) 0.9
To solve this problem, let's use the concept of probability and the fact that events A and B are independent.

We know that the probability of at least one of the events A or B occurring is 0.96. This means that the complement of this event (neither A nor B occurs) has a probability of 1 - 0.96 = 0.04.

Since events A and B are independent, the probability of neither A nor B occurring is the product of their individual probabilities: P(A') * P(B') = 0.04.

We are given that P(A) = 0.6. Therefore, P(A') = 1 - P(A) = 1 - 0.6 = 0.4.

Now, let's find the probability of event B occurring. We can use the formula:

P(A') * P(B') = 0.04

0.4 * P(B') = 0.04

Dividing both sides by 0.4, we get:

P(B') = 0.04 / 0.4 = 0.1

Since P(B') is the probability of event B not occurring, we can find the probability of event B occurring by subtracting P(B') from 1:

P(B) = 1 - P(B') = 1 - 0.1 = 0.9

Therefore, the probability that event B occurs is 0.9.

The correct answer choice is (E) 0.9.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is(E) 0.9

To solve this problem, let's break it down step by step:

Now, we know that 75% of the men preferred red cars over green cars. Therefore, 25% of the men preferred green cars.

(1/4) * 0.4x = 10

0.1x = 10

If the area of each of triangle is 70 square feet, what was the perimeter (in feet) of the original piece of square cloth? Answer Choices: (A) 56 (B) 58 (C) 60 (D) 62 (E) 64
To solve this problem, let's start by finding the dimensions of the rectangular piece of cloth.

Since the area of each triangle is 70 square feet, and a triangle's area is given by the formula A = (1/2) * base * height, we can set up the equation:

70 = (1/2) * base * height

Since the two triangles are congruent, their bases and heights are equal. Let's call the base and height of each triangle "x".

70 = (1/2) * x * x
140 = x^2
x = √140
x ≈ 11.83

So, the dimensions of the rectangular piece of cloth are approximately 11.83 feet by 11.83 feet.

Now, let's find the perimeter of the original square cloth. Since one edge was trimmed by 4 feet, the original side length of the square cloth is 11.83 + 4 = 15.83 feet.

The perimeter of a square is given by the formula P = 4 * side length, so the perimeter of the original square cloth is:

P = 4 * 15.83
P ≈ 63.32

Rounding to the nearest whole number, the perimeter of the original square cloth is approximately 63 feet.

If the weight of the coin is 30 grams and the volume of aluminum in the alloy equals that of silver, what will be the weight of a coin measuring 1 x 30 mm made of pure aluminum if silver is twice as heavy as aluminum? Answer Choices: (A) 36 grams (B) 40 grams (C) 42 grams (D) 48 grams (E) 50 grams
To solve this problem, let's first find the volume of the coin made of the aluminum-silver alloy. The volume of a cylinder (which the coin resembles) is given by the formula V = πr^2h, where r is the radius and h is the height (or thickness in this case).

Given that the diameter of the coin is 15 mm, the radius (r) is half of that, which is 7.5 mm or 0.75 cm. The height (h) is given as 2 mm or 0.2 cm.

Using these values, we can calculate the volume of the coin:

V = π(0.75 cm)^2(0.2 cm)
V ≈ 0.3535 cm^3

Since the volume of aluminum in the alloy is equal to that of silver, the volume of each metal is half of the total volume of the coin:

Volume of aluminum = 0.5 * 0.3535 cm^3 = 0.1768 cm^3

Now, we know that the weight of silver is twice that of aluminum. Let's assume the weight of aluminum is x grams. Therefore, the weight of silver would be 2x grams.

Since the density of a substance is given by the formula density = mass/volume, we can set up the following equations:

Density of aluminum = x grams / 0.1768 cm^3
Density of silver = 2x grams / 0.1768 cm^3

Given that the weight of the coin is 30 grams, we can set up another equation:

Weight of aluminum + Weight of silver = 30 grams

Substituting the density equations into the weight equation, we get:

(x grams / 0.1768 cm^3) + (2x grams / 0.1768 cm^3) = 30 grams

Combining like terms, we have:

3x grams / 0.1768 cm^3 = 30 grams

Now, let's solve for x:

3x grams = 30 grams * 0.1768 cm^3
3x grams = 5.304 grams * cm^3

Dividing both sides by 3, we find:

x grams = 5.304 grams * cm^3 / 3
x grams ≈ 1.768 grams * cm^3

Hoses A and B spout water at different constant rates, and hose A can fill a certain pool in 8 hours. Hose A filled the pool alone for the first 2 hours and the two hoses, working together, then finished filling the pool in another 3 hours. How many hours would it have taken hose B, working alone, to fill the entire pool? Answer Choices: (A) 8 (B) 15 (C) 12 (D) 6 (E) 3
To solve this problem, let's first determine the rate at which hose A fills the pool. Since hose A can fill the pool in 8 hours, its rate is 1 pool per 8 hours, or 1/8 of the pool per hour.

Now, let's consider the time when hose A filled the pool alone for the first 2 hours. In these 2 hours, hose A filled 2/8 = 1/4 of the pool.

Next, let's determine the rate at which both hoses A and B fill the pool when working together. We know that they finished filling the pool in 3 hours, so their combined rate is 1 pool per 3 hours, or 1/3 of the pool per hour.

Since hose A filled 1/4 of the pool in the first 2 hours, the remaining 3/4 of the pool was filled by both hoses in the next 3 hours. Therefore, their combined rate is 3/4 divided by 3, which simplifies to 1/4 of the pool per hour.

Now, let's find the rate at which hose B fills the pool when working alone. Since the combined rate of both hoses is 1/4 of the pool per hour, and we know that hose A's rate is 1/8 of the pool per hour, we can subtract hose A's rate from the combined rate to find hose B's rate.

Hose B's rate = Combined rate - Hose A's rate
Hose B's rate = 1/4 - 1/8
Hose B's rate = 2/8 - 1/8
Hose B's rate = 1/8 of the pool per hour.

Now that we know hose B's rate is 1/8 of the pool per hour, we can determine how long it would take for hose B to fill the entire pool by setting up the equation:

1 pool = (1/8) pool per hour * time

Simplifying the equation, we have:
1 = (1/8) * time

To solve for time, we multiply both sides of the equation by 8:
8 = time

Therefore, it would take hose B, working alone, 8 hours to fill the entire pool.

The correct answer is (A) 8.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is(A) 8

To solve this problem, let's consider the net gain or loss for each flip. 

When the coin lands on heads, Christopher gives $2 to Jonathan, resulting in a net loss of $2. 
When the coin lands on tails, Jonathan gives $3 to Christopher, resulting in a net gain of $3. 

Since the total net gain or loss is zero after flipping the coin twenty times, the number of times the coin landed on heads must be equal to the number of times it landed on tails. 

Let's assume the coin landed on heads x times. Therefore, it landed on tails (20 - x) times. 

The net gain from the heads is -2x, and the net gain from the tails is 3(20 - x). 

Setting up the equation: 
-2x + 3(20 - x) = 0 

Simplifying the equation: 
-2x + 60 - 3x = 0 
-5x + 60 = 0 
-5x = -60 
x = 12 

Therefore, the coin landed on heads 12 times. 

The answer is (E) 12.

(a - b) / (a + b) = (a - b)^2

(a - b) = (a - b)^2 * (a + b)

The number of water lilies on a certain lake doubles every two days. If there is exactly one water lily on the lake, it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies. In how many days will the lake be fully covered with lilies, if initially there were 64 water lilies on it? Answer Choices: (A) 15 (B) 28 (C) 30 (D) 53 (E) 59
To solve this problem, we can use the concept of exponential growth. 

We know that the number of water lilies doubles every two days. Let's represent the number of days it takes for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies as "x."

Initially, there were 64 water lilies on the lake. Since the number of water lilies doubles every two days, after two days, there will be 64 * 2 = 128 water lilies.

After four days, there will be 128 * 2 = 256 water lilies.

We can see that the number of water lilies follows the pattern: 64, 128, 256, ...

We need to find the value of "x" when the number of water lilies reaches or exceeds the total number of water lilies needed to fully cover the lake, which is 60 days.

Let's write the equation: 64 * 2^(x/2) ≥ 60

Dividing both sides of the equation by 64, we get: 2^(x/2) ≥ 60/64

Simplifying further, we have: 2^(x/2) ≥ 15/16

Taking the logarithm of both sides, we get: x/2 ≥ log(15/16) / log(2)

Using a calculator, we find that log(15/16) / log(2) ≈ -0.043

Multiplying both sides by 2, we have: x ≥ -0.086

Since the number of days cannot be negative, we can disregard the negative value.

Therefore, the lake will be fully covered with water lilies in approximately 0.086 * 2 = 0.172 days.

Since we cannot have a fraction of a day, we round up to the nearest whole number.

Hence, the lake will be fully covered with lilies in 1 day.

Therefore, the correct answer is (A) 15.

An exam is given in a certain class. The average (arithmetic mean) of the highest score and the lowest score is equal to x. If the average score for the entire class is equal to y and there are z students in the class, where z > 5, then in terms of x, y, and z, what is the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers? Answer Choices: (A)  (zy – 2x) /z (B)  (zy – 2) /z (C)  (zx – y) / (z – 2)  (D)  (zy – 2x) / (z -2)  (E)  (zy – x) / (z + 2) 
To find the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers, we need to consider the sum of all the scores excluding the highest and lowest, and then divide it by the number of students minus 2 (since we are excluding 2 scores).

Let's denote the highest score as H and the lowest score as L. The sum of all the scores in the class is y * z (average score multiplied by the number of students).

Now, the sum of all the scores excluding the highest and lowest is (y * z) - H - L.

We are given that the average of the highest and lowest scores is x, so we can write the equation:

(x + x) / 2 = x
2x = 2x

This means that the highest and lowest scores are both equal to x.

Substituting this into the sum of all the scores excluding the highest and lowest, we get:

(y * z) - x - x = (y * z) - 2x

Finally, to find the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers, we divide this sum by the number of students minus 2:

Average score = [(y * z) - 2x] / (z - 2)

Therefore, the correct answer is (D) (zy - 2x) / (z - 2).

Winson runs from his home to his school at an average speed of 10 miles/hr, and then walks home along the same route at an average speed of 5 miles/hr. If the whole journey took one hour, how many miles is his home from his school? Answer Choices: (A) 9 (B) 6 (C) 4 (D) 3 (E) 2
To solve this problem, let's use the concept of average speed and the formula: 

Average Speed = Total Distance / Total Time

Let's assume the distance from Winson's home to his school is 'd' miles.

When Winson runs from his home to school at an average speed of 10 miles/hr, the time taken can be calculated as:
Time1 = Distance1 / Speed1 = d / 10

When Winson walks from school to home at an average speed of 5 miles/hr, the time taken can be calculated as:
Time2 = Distance2 / Speed2 = d / 5

According to the problem, the total time taken for the whole journey is 1 hour. So, we can write the equation:
Time1 + Time2 = 1

Substituting the values of Time1 and Time2, we get:
d / 10 + d / 5 = 1

To simplify the equation, we can multiply through by 10 to eliminate the denominators:
2d + 4d = 10

Combining like terms, we have:
6d = 10

Dividing both sides by 6, we find:
d = 10 / 6 = 5 / 3

Therefore, the distance from Winson's home to his school is 5/3 miles, which is approximately 1.67 miles.

To solve this problem, let's assume the two numbers are x and y. We are given two pieces of information:

1. The difference between the squares of the two numbers is 256000. This can be written as:
   x^2 - y^2 = 256000

2. The sum of the numbers is 1000. This can be written as:
   x + y = 1000

Now, let's solve these equations simultaneously to find the values of x and y.

From equation 2, we can express y in terms of x:
y = 1000 - x

Substituting this value of y in equation 1, we get:
x^2 - (1000 - x)^2 = 256000

Expanding and simplifying the equation:
x^2 - (1000^2 - 2000x + x^2) = 256000
x^2 - 1000000 + 2000x - x^2 = 256000
2000x - 1000000 = 256000
2000x = 1256000
x = 628

Substituting this value of x in equation 2, we can find y:
y = 1000 - x
y = 1000 - 628
y = 372

Therefore, the numbers are 628 and 372.

To form a quadrilateral, we need to select 4 points out of the 6 given points (A, B, C, D, E, and F). Since F is at the center of the pentagon, any quadrilateral formed with F will always be the same. Therefore, we can consider two cases:

Case 1: F is not selected.
In this case, we need to select 4 points out of the remaining 5 points (A, B, C, D, and E). The number of ways to do this is given by the combination formula: C(5, 4) = 5.

Case 2: F is selected.
Since F is fixed, we only need to select 3 points out of the remaining 5 points (A, B, C, D, and E). The number of ways to do this is given by the combination formula: C(5, 3) = 10.

Therefore, the total number of different quadrilaterals that can be formed is 5 (from Case 1) + 10 (from Case 2) = 15.

Let's assume the length of the rectangular plot is L and the width is W. The perimeter of a rectangle is given by the formula: 2(L + W) = 340.

To solve this problem, we can set up an equation based on the given information.

Now, we want to add additional gallons of orange juice to make it 60% of the soft drink. Let's say we add y gallons of orange juice.

The total amount of soft drink after adding the additional orange juice would be x + y gallons.

0.4x + y = 0.6(x + y)

0.4x + y = 0.6x + 0.6y

0.6y - y = 0.6x - 0.4x

0.2y = 0.2x

y = x

This means that the additional gallons of orange juice we need to add is equal to the total amount of soft drink we want to make.

94st data
In a survey of students, each student selected from a list of 10 songs the 2 songs that the student liked best. If each song was selected 5 times, how many students were surveyed? Answer Choices: (A) 96 (B) 48 (C) 32 (D) 25 (E) 18
To solve this problem, we can use the concept of combinations. Since each student selected 2 songs from a list of 10, we can calculate the number of ways to choose 2 songs out of 10, which is denoted as "10 choose 2" or written as 10C2.

The formula for combinations is given by: nCr = n! / (r!(n-r)!), where n is the total number of items and r is the number of items to be chosen.

Using this formula, we can calculate 10C2 as follows:

10C2 = 10! / (2!(10-2)!)
     = 10! / (2!8!)
     = (10 * 9 * 8!) / (2! * 8!)
     = (10 * 9) / 2!
     = (10 * 9) / (2 * 1)
     = 90 / 2
     = 45

Therefore, 10C2 is equal to 45. This means that there are 45 different pairs of songs that a student can choose.

Now, since each song was selected 5 times, we can divide the total number of song selections by the number of pairs to find the number of students surveyed:

Total song selections = 10 songs * 5 selections per song = 50

Number of students surveyed = Total song selections / Number of pairs
                          = 50 / 45
                          = 10/9

Since the number of students surveyed must be a whole number, we can round up to the nearest whole number, which is 2.

Therefore, the correct answer is (B) 48 students.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is(B) 48

To find the total bus fare for 4 adults and 3 children between Ranchi and Patna, we need to calculate the individual fares for each group and then add them together.

The fare for one adult is Rs. 140, and the fare for one child is half of that, which is Rs. 70 (140/2).

For 4 adults, the total fare would be 4 times the fare for one adult: 4 * Rs. 140 = Rs. 560.

For 3 children, the total fare would be 3 times the fare for one child: 3 * Rs. 70 = Rs. 210.

Now, we add the fares for adults and children together: Rs. 560 + Rs. 210 = Rs. 770.

Therefore, the total bus fare for 4 adults and 3 children between Ranchi and Patna is Rs. 770.

Suppose for any real number x, [x] denotes the greatest integer less than or equal to x. Let L(x,y) = [x] + [y] + [x + y] and R(x,y) = [2x] + [2y]. Then it is impossible to find any two positive real numbers x and y for which Answer Choices: (A) L (x,y)  = R (x,y)  (B) L (x,y)  ≠ R (x,y)  (C) L (x,y)  < R (x,y)  (D) L (x,y)  < R (x,y)  (E) None
Let's analyze the given expressions and answer choices.

First, let's consider the expression L(x, y) = [x] + [y] + [x + y]. The greatest integer function [x] returns the largest integer less than or equal to x. Therefore, [x] + [y] + [x + y] will always be an integer since it is the sum of three integers.

Next, let's consider the expression R(x, y) = [2x] + [2y]. Similar to before, [2x] and [2y] will also be integers since they are the greatest integers less than or equal to 2x and 2y, respectively.

Now, let's analyze the answer choices:

(A) L(x, y) = R(x, y): This implies that [x] + [y] + [x + y] = [2x] + [2y]. Since both sides of the equation are integers, this equation can be satisfied by choosing appropriate values for x and y. Therefore, this answer choice is possible.

(B) L(x, y) ≠ R(x, y): This means that [x] + [y] + [x + y] is not equal to [2x] + [2y]. Since both sides of the equation are integers, it is possible to find values for x and y that make this inequality true. Therefore, this answer choice is possible.

(C) L(x, y) < R(x, y): This implies that [x] + [y] + [x + y] is less than [2x] + [2y]. Since both sides of the inequality are integers, it is possible to find values for x and y that satisfy this inequality. Therefore, this answer choice is possible.

(D) L(x, y) < R(x, y): This is the same as answer choice (C) and is a duplicate. It should be disregarded.

(E) None: Since we have shown that all the answer choices are possible, this answer choice is incorrect.

In conclusion, answer choices (A), (B), and (C) are all possible, and the correct answer is (E) None.

At what price should the Karan mark a sewing machine that costs him Rs. 1200/- so that even after offering a 20% discount, he makes 20% profit? Answer Choices: (A) 1,879 (B) 1,875 (C) 1,876 (D) 1,872 (E) 1,800
To find the price at which Karan should mark the sewing machine, we need to consider both the cost price and the desired profit.

Let's start by calculating the selling price after offering a 20% discount. The selling price will be 80% of the original price since a 20% discount means the customer pays only 80% of the original price.

Selling price = 80% of the original price
Selling price = 0.8 * original price

Now, we want Karan to make a 20% profit on the cost price. To calculate the selling price that includes a 20% profit, we need to add 20% of the cost price to the cost price.

Selling price with 20% profit = cost price + 20% of the cost price
Selling price with 20% profit = cost price + 0.2 * cost price
Selling price with 20% profit = 1.2 * cost price

Given that the cost price is Rs. 1200/-, we can substitute this value into the equation:

Selling price with 20% profit = 1.2 * 1200
Selling price with 20% profit = 1440

Now, we know that the selling price after offering a 20% discount should be Rs. 1440/-. Let's find the original price (marked price) before the discount:

Original price = Selling price after discount / (1 - discount percentage)
Original price = 1440 / (1 - 0.2)
Original price = 1440 / 0.8
Original price = 1800

Therefore, the correct answer is (E) Rs. 1800.

Answer Choices: (A) 126 (B) 77 (C) 88 (D) 66 (E) 54
Let's solve the problem step by step.

Let's assume the train fare between Agra and Aligarh for one person is 'x' rupees.

According to the given information, the bus fare for two persons is four-thirds the train fare for one person. Therefore, the bus fare for two persons is (4/3) * x.

Now, let's calculate the total fare paid by 6 persons traveling by bus. Since each bus fare is for two persons, the total fare paid by 6 persons is (6/2) * (4/3) * x = 4x.

Similarly, the total fare paid by 8 persons traveling by train is 8x.

According to the problem, the total fare paid by 6 persons traveling by bus and 8 persons traveling by train is Rs. 1512. So, we can write the equation as:

4x + 8x = 1512

Combining like terms, we get:

12x = 1512

Dividing both sides by 12, we find:

x = 1512/12

x = 126

Therefore, the train fare between Agra and Aligarh for one person is Rs. 126.

Hence, the correct answer is (A) 126.

Let A and B be independent events with P (A) = 0.2 and P(B) = 0.8. Find P(A/B)? Answer Choices: (A) 0.2 (B) 0.4 (C) 0.6 (D) 1.2 (E) 1.5
To find P(A/B), we can use the formula for conditional probability:

P(A/B) = P(A ∩ B) / P(B)

Since A and B are independent events, P(A ∩ B) = P(A) * P(B).

Given that P(A) = 0.2 and P(B) = 0.8, we can substitute these values into the formula:

P(A/B) = (0.2 * 0.8) / 0.8

Simplifying the expression:

P(A/B) = 0.16 / 0.8

P(A/B) = 0.2

Therefore, the correct answer is (A) 0.2.

To find the value of m, we can use the fact that the sum of the roots of a quadratic equation is equal to the negation of the coefficient of the linear term (mx). 

In this case, we know that one of the roots is 1.5. Let's call the other root r. 

The sum of the roots is given by 1.5 + r. 

According to the sum of roots formula, this sum should be equal to -m. 

So, we have the equation 1.5 + r = -m. 

Now, we need to find the value of m. 

To do that, we can substitute the given equation x^2 + mx + 22 = 0 into the quadratic formula: 

x = (-b ± √(b^2 - 4ac)) / (2a)

In this case, a = 1, b = m, and c = 22. 

Since we know that one of the roots is 1.5, we can substitute x = 1.5 into the quadratic formula: 

1.5 = (-m ± √(m^2 - 4(1)(22))) / (2(1))

3 = -m ± √(m^2 - 88)

Now, let's consider the positive square root: 

3 = -m + √(m^2 - 88)

Squaring both sides of the equation, we have: 

9 = m^2 - 88

Rearranging the equation, we get: 

m^2 = 97

Taking the square root of both sides, we find: 

m = ±√97

Since we are looking for a specific value of m, we can disregard the negative square root. 

Therefore, m = √97 ≈ 9.85

If train is traveling at 120 mile an hour, how long will it take to pass completely through the tunnel ? Answer Choices: (A) 43 seconds (B) 39 seconds (C) 20 seconds (D) 33 seconds (E) 55 seconds
To solve this problem, we need to find the time it takes for the train to pass completely through the tunnel. 

First, let's convert the train's speed from miles per hour to miles per second. Since there are 60 minutes in an hour and 60 seconds in a minute, we can divide 120 miles per hour by 60 to get the speed in miles per minute: 

120 miles/hour ÷ 60 minutes/hour = 2 miles/minute.

Next, we need to convert the speed from miles per minute to miles per second. Since there are 60 seconds in a minute, we can divide 2 miles per minute by 60 to get the speed in miles per second: 

2 miles/minute ÷ 60 seconds/minute = 1/30 miles/second.

Now, we know that the train takes 3 seconds to enter the tunnel, which is 1 mile long. Therefore, it takes 1/3 miles per second to enter the tunnel. 

To find the time it takes to pass completely through the tunnel, we can subtract the time it takes to enter the tunnel from the total time it takes to travel 1 mile at the train's speed: 

1 mile ÷ (1/30 miles/second) = 30 seconds.

To find the probability that the question is answered correctly, but not via cheating, we need to consider the probabilities of each friend answering correctly and subtract the probability of cheating.

Let's denote the events as follows:
A: Alan answers correctly (1/5 probability)
R: Roger answers correctly (2/3 probability)
P: Peter answers correctly (5/6 probability)

The probability that the question is answered correctly, but not via cheating, can be calculated as:
P(A and not R and not P) = P(A) - P(A and R) - P(A and P) + P(A and R and P)

P(A and not R and not P) = (1/5) - (1/5 * 2/3) - (1/5 * 5/6) + (1/5 * 2/3 * 5/6)

P(A and not R and not P) = (3 - 2 - 5 + 2)/30

P(A and not R and not P) = -2/30

A can construct a wall in 40 min and B can construct the wall in 45 min. How many hours is needed to contruct a wall if both the person working together. Answer Choices: (A) 20 min (B) 22 min (C) 23 min (D) 21 min (E) 20 min
To solve this problem, we can use the concept of work rates. The work rate of a person is the amount of work they can complete in a given time.

Let's say the total work required to construct the wall is represented by "1." 

A can construct the wall in 40 minutes, so their work rate is 1 wall / 40 minutes = 1/40 walls per minute.
B can construct the wall in 45 minutes, so their work rate is 1 wall / 45 minutes = 1/45 walls per minute.

When A and B work together, their work rates add up. So the combined work rate is (1/40 + 1/45) walls per minute.

To find the time needed to construct the wall when they work together, we can use the formula:

Time = 1 / Combined work rate

Time = 1 / (1/40 + 1/45)

To simplify this expression, we can find the least common multiple (LCM) of 40 and 45, which is 360. 

Time = 1 / (9/360 + 8/360)

Time = 1 / (17/360)

Time = 360 / 17

Time ≈ 21.18 minutes

Since the answer choices are given in minutes, we round the answer to the nearest minute.

Therefore, the correct answer is (D) 21 min.

120st data
Peter wants to find 10 additional people to form a scavenger hunt team with him. If he has 10 friends who would like to participate, how many choices does he have for forming his team? Answer Choices: (A) 0 (B) 1 (C) 2 (D) 3 (E) 4
To find the number of choices Peter has for forming his team, we need to consider the number of ways he can select 10 additional people from his 10 friends.

This problem can be solved using combinations, specifically the concept of "n choose k." In this case, Peter has 10 friends, and he needs to choose 10 additional people to form his team. Therefore, the answer is 10 choose 10, which can be written as 10C10.

The formula for combinations is given by:

nCk = n! / (k! * (n-k)!)

Plugging in the values, we have:

10C10 = 10! / (10! * (10-10)!)

Simplifying further:

10C10 = 10! / (10! * 0!)

Since 0! (zero factorial) is defined as 1, we have:

10C10 = 10! / (10! * 1)

Now, we can cancel out the 10! terms:

10C10 = 1 / 1

Therefore, the number of choices Peter has for forming his team is 1.

Hence, the correct answer is (B) 1.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is(B) 1.

A train running at a speed of 100 miles/hour, takes 10 hours to reach its destination. After covering quarter of the distance, it starts raining and the train has to be slowed to speed of 75 miles/hour. What is the total journey duration? Answer Choices: (A) 10 (B) 11.5 (C) 12.5 (D) 13.5 (E) 15
To solve this problem, we need to calculate the time it takes for the train to cover the first quarter of the distance and the remaining three-quarters of the distance separately.

Let's start with the first quarter of the distance. Since the train is traveling at a speed of 100 miles/hour, it will cover a quarter of the distance in 10 hours / 4 = 2.5 hours.

Now, let's calculate the time it takes for the train to cover the remaining three-quarters of the distance. The train is now traveling at a speed of 75 miles/hour. To cover three-quarters of the distance, it will take (10 hours - 2.5 hours) = 7.5 hours.

Finally, we add the time taken for the first quarter and the time taken for the remaining three-quarters to find the total journey duration: 2.5 hours + 7.5 hours = 10 hours.

Therefore, the correct answer is (A) 10.

A straight picket fence is composed of x pickets each of which is 1/2 inch wide. If there are 6 inches of space between each pair of pickets, which of the following represents the length of fence in feet? Answer Choices: (A) 13x/2 (B) 13x/2 - 6 (C) 13x/24 (D)  (13x+1) /24 (E)  (13x-12) /24
To find the length of the fence in feet, we need to consider the width of each picket and the space between them. 

Let's break down the problem step by step:

1. The width of each picket is given as 1/2 inch.
2. There are x pickets in total.
3. The space between each pair of pickets is 6 inches.

To calculate the total length of the fence, we need to consider the width of the pickets and the space between them. 

The total width of the pickets can be calculated as x * (1/2) inches.

The total width of the spaces between the pickets can be calculated as (x - 1) * 6 inches. (Note that there are (x - 1) spaces between x pickets.)

To find the total length of the fence, we add the total width of the pickets and the total width of the spaces:

Total length = Total width of pickets + Total width of spaces
Total length = x * (1/2) inches + (x - 1) * 6 inches

Now, we need to convert the length from inches to feet. Since there are 12 inches in a foot, we divide the total length by 12 to get the length in feet:

Total length in feet = (x * (1/2) inches + (x - 1) * 6 inches) / 12

Simplifying the expression further:

Total length in feet = (x/2 + 6x - 6) / 12
Total length in feet = (13x - 12) / 24

Therefore, the correct answer is (E) (13x - 12) / 24.

To determine the probability that Mr. Jain selected the winning horse, we need to consider the total number of possible outcomes and the number of favorable outcomes.

Total number of possible outcomes: Since Mr. Jain selects two horses out of five, the total number of possible outcomes is given by the combination formula, denoted as C(5, 2), which is equal to 10.

Number of favorable outcomes: Out of the five horses, only one can be the winning horse. Since Mr. Jain selects two horses, there are two ways in which he can select the winning horse.

Therefore, the number of favorable outcomes is 2.

Now, we can calculate the probability by dividing the number of favorable outcomes by the total number of possible outcomes:

Probability = Number of favorable outcomes / Total number of possible outcomes
Probability = 2 / 10
Probability = 1/5

Hence, the probability that Mr. Jain selected the winning horse is 1/5.

To solve this problem, let's assume that there are 100 students at Daifu University. 

Given that 24% of all students are members of both the chess club and the swim team, we can calculate the number of students in this intersection as 24% of 100, which is 24 students.

Now, let's find the number of students who are only members of the swim team. We know that 20% of the swim team members are not members of the chess club. So, if we assume that the swim team has x members, then 20% of x are not in the chess club. This can be written as 0.2x.

Since we already have 24 students who are members of both the chess club and the swim team, the number of students who are only members of the swim team is x - 24 - 0.2x.

Now, we can set up an equation to find the value of x:

x - 24 - 0.2x = 0

Simplifying the equation, we get:

0.8x - 24 = 0

0.8x = 24

x = 24 / 0.8

x = 30

So, the swim team has 30 members.

To find the percentage of all Daifu students who are members of the swim team, we divide the number of swim team members (30) by the total number of students (100) and multiply by 100:

(30 / 100) * 100 = 30%

Therefore, the answer is (B) 30%.

In IPL season, Sachin current batting average is 51. In the finals, he scores 78 runs, then is batting average will be 54. Find out the total number of matches played by Sachin in this season. Answer Choices: (A) 6 (B) 8 (C) 9 (D) 10 (E) 11
To solve this problem, we can use the formula for batting average:

Batting Average = Total Runs / Total Innings

Let's assume that Sachin played "x" matches in the season. Since each match consists of two innings, the total number of innings Sachin played would be 2x.

Given that Sachin's current batting average is 51, we can write the equation:

51 = Total Runs / (2x)

To find the total runs, we need to multiply the batting average by the number of innings:

Total Runs = 51 * (2x)

In the finals, Sachin scored 78 runs, so his new total runs would be:

Total Runs = 51 * (2x) + 78

After the finals, his new batting average is 54, so we can write another equation:

54 = (Total Runs + 78) / (2x + 2)

Now we can substitute the value of Total Runs from the first equation into the second equation:

54 = (51 * (2x) + 78 + 78) / (2x + 2)

Simplifying this equation:

54 = (102x + 156) / (2x + 2)

Multiplying both sides by (2x + 2) to eliminate the denominator:

54 * (2x + 2) = 102x + 156

108x + 108 = 102x + 156

6x = 48

x = 8

Therefore, Sachin played a total of 8 matches in the season.

The answer is (B) 8.

If a man rows at the rate of 4 kmph in still water and his rate against the current is 2 kmph, then the man's rate along the current is: Answer Choices: (A) 15 kmph (B) 6 kmph (C) 12 kmph (D) 14 kmph (E) 6 kmph
To solve this problem, we can use the concept of relative velocity. 

Let's assume the speed of the current is 'c' kmph. 

When the man rows against the current, his effective speed is reduced by the speed of the current. So, his speed against the current is (4 - c) kmph. 

Similarly, when the man rows along the current, his effective speed is increased by the speed of the current. So, his speed along the current is (4 + c) kmph. 

Given that the man's speed against the current is 2 kmph, we can set up the equation: 

4 - c = 2 

Solving this equation, we find that c = 2 kmph. 

Now, we can substitute the value of c into the equation for the man's speed along the current: 

4 + c = 4 + 2 = 6 kmph 

Therefore, the man's rate along the current is 6 kmph. 

Hence, the correct answer is (E) 6 kmph.

There is well of depth 30m and frog is at bottom of the well. He jumps 3m up one day and falls back 2m down the same day. How many days will it take for the frog to come out of the well? Answer Choices: (A) 25 days (B) 26 days (C) 27 days (D) 28 days (E) 29 days
To determine the number of days it will take for the frog to come out of the well, we need to calculate how many jumps it will take for the frog to reach the top.

Each day, the frog jumps 3m up and falls 2m down. Therefore, the frog makes a net progress of 3m - 2m = 1m per day.

Since the well is 30m deep, the frog needs to make 30m of net progress to reach the top.

To calculate the number of days needed, we divide the total distance by the net progress per day:

30m / 1m = 30 days.

Therefore, it will take the frog 30 days to come out of the well.

The correct answer choice is (E) 29 days.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is(E) 29 days.

Allen's distance: 2d = 54 × (d/54 + d/54)

142st data
The manufacturer of tyres is offering a 20% discount on the price of its tubeless tyres. Some retailers are offering additional discounts. If a retailer offers an additional 20% discount, then what is the total discount available at that retailer? Answer Choices: (A) 10% (B) 25% (C) 28% (D) 30% (E) 36%
To calculate the total discount available at the retailer, we need to find the combined discount of the manufacturer's discount and the additional discount offered by the retailer.

Let's start with the manufacturer's discount of 20%. To find the price after the manufacturer's discount, we subtract 20% of the original price from the original price:

Price after manufacturer's discount = Original price - (20% of original price)
= Original price - (0.20 * Original price)
= Original price * (1 - 0.20)
= Original price * 0.80

Now, the retailer offers an additional 20% discount on the price after the manufacturer's discount. To find the price after the retailer's discount, we subtract 20% of the price after the manufacturer's discount from the price after the manufacturer's discount:

Price after retailer's discount = Price after manufacturer's discount - (20% of price after manufacturer's discount)
= (Original price * 0.80) - (0.20 * (Original price * 0.80))
= (Original price * 0.80) - (0.20 * Original price * 0.80)
= Original price * (0.80 - 0.20 * 0.80)
= Original price * (0.80 - 0.16)
= Original price * 0.64

To find the total discount percentage, we need to calculate the difference between the original price and the price after the retailer's discount, and then express it as a percentage of the original price:

Total discount percentage = (Original price - Price after retailer's discount) / Original price * 100
= (Original price - (Original price * 0.64)) / Original price * 100
= (Original price * (1 - 0.64)) / Original price * 100
= (Original price * 0.36) / Original price * 100
= 0.36 * 100
= 36%

Therefore, the total discount available at the retailer is 36%. The correct answer choice is (E) 36%.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is(E) 36%

At an election meeting 10 speakers are to address the meeting. The only protocol to be observed is that whenever they speak the pm should speak before the mp and the mp should speak before the mla. In how many ways can the meeting be held? Answer Choices: (A) 10!/3 (B) 10!/6 (C) 10!/2 (D) 10!/4 (E) 10!/5
To solve this problem, we can break it down into three steps:

Step 1: Determine the order in which the Prime Minister (PM), Member of Parliament (MP), and Member of Legislative Assembly (MLA) speak.

Since the PM must speak before the MP, and the MP must speak before the MLA, we have three options for the first speaker: PM, MP, or MLA. Once the first speaker is chosen, the remaining two speakers must follow the given order. Therefore, there are 3! = 3 × 2 × 1 = 6 ways to determine the order in which the PM, MP, and MLA speak.

Step 2: Determine the order in which the remaining 7 speakers (who are not the PM, MP, or MLA) speak.

Since these 7 speakers are not subject to any specific order, we can arrange them in 7! = 7 × 6 × 5 × 4 × 3 × 2 × 1 = 5040 ways.

Step 3: Multiply the results from Step 1 and Step 2 to find the total number of ways the meeting can be held.

The total number of ways is given by 6 × 5040 = 30,240.

Therefore, the correct answer is (B) 10!/6.

Note: The answer choices provided are in terms of factorials, which represent the product of a number and all positive integers less than it.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is(B) 10!/6.

A jeep travels a certain distance taking 6 hours in the forward journey. During the return journey, it increased its speed by 12km/hr and took 4 hours. What is the distance travelled by the jeep? Answer Choices: (A) 126km (B) 144km (C) 127km (D) 228km (E) 128km
To solve this problem, we can use the formula: 

Distance = Speed × Time

Let's assume the initial speed of the jeep during the forward journey is 'x' km/hr. 

During the forward journey, the jeep takes 6 hours to travel a certain distance, so we have:

Distance = x km/hr × 6 hours = 6x km

During the return journey, the jeep increases its speed by 12 km/hr, so the speed becomes 'x + 12' km/hr. The time taken for the return journey is 4 hours, so we have:

Distance = (x + 12) km/hr × 4 hours = 4(x + 12) km

Since the distance traveled during the forward and return journeys is the same, we can equate the two expressions for distance:

6x = 4(x + 12)

Simplifying the equation:

6x = 4x + 48
2x = 48
x = 24

Now, we can substitute the value of 'x' back into one of the distance expressions to find the distance traveled:

Distance = 6x = 6 × 24 = 144 km

Therefore, the correct answer is (B) 144 km.
Therefore, among A through E, the answer is(B) 144km.

To solve this problem, let's break it down step by step:

Step 1: Let's assume the three-digit number is represented as ABC, where A, B, and C are the digits.

Step 2: We are given that the sum of the digits is 17, so we can write the equation as A + B + C = 17.

Step 3: We are also given that the sum of the squares of the digits is 109, so we can write the equation as A^2 + B^2 + C^2 = 109.

Step 4: Now, let's consider the number obtained by subtracting 495 from the original number. It will be represented as CBA.

Step 5: We can write the equation for this number as 100C + 10B + A - 495 = 100A + 10B + C.

Step 6: Simplifying the equation, we get 99C - 99A = 495.

Step 7: Dividing both sides of the equation by 99, we have C - A = 5.

Step 8: Now, we have two equations:
   A + B + C = 17   (Equation 1)
   C - A = 5   (Equation 2)

Step 9: Solving Equation 2 for C, we get C = A + 5.

Step 10: Substituting C = A + 5 into Equation 1, we have A + B + (A + 5) = 17.

Step 11: Simplifying the equation, we get 2A + B = 12.

Step 12: Since A, B, and C are digits, the possible values for A and B are limited. By trying different combinations, we find that A = 3 and B = 6 satisfy the equation.

Step 13: Substituting A = 3 and B = 6 into Equation 2, we get C = 3 + 5 = 8.

Step 14: Therefore, the number ABC is 368.
